RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The Sage Valmiki, chief among the munis and the most eloquent of men, constantly engaged in the practice of selfcontrol and the study of the holy scriptures, enquired of Shri Narada:--
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	"Who is there in the world to-day, endowed with excellent and heroic qualities, who is versed in all the duties of life, grateful, truthful, firm in his vows, an actor of many parts, benevolent to all beings, learned, eloquent, handsome, patient, slow to anger, one who is truly great; who is free from envy and when excited to wrath can strike terror into the hearts of celestial beings?
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	O Sage, I would hear of such a man from you, who art able to describe him to me."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Narada, acquainted with the past, the present and the future, pleased with the words of the Sage Valmiki, answered him saying:--
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	"Rare indeed are those, endowed with the qualities you have enumerated, yet I can tell you of such a one.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Born in the family of Ikshvaku, he is named Rama; one renowned, fully self-controlled, valorous and illustrious, the Lord of All.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Wise, conversant with the ethical code, eloquent, fortunate, a slayer of his foes, broad-shouldered, long-armed, possessing a conch-shaped neck and prominent chin, eminent in archery, with a muscular body, arms extending to the knees, and a noble head and brow; of mighty prowess; possessing well-proportioned limbs and skin of bluish tint, one renowned for his virtue; of prominent eyes, deep-chested, bearing auspicious marks; one who protects those who take refuge in him and is ever-mindful of the good of those dependent on him; true to his promises, benevolent to his subjects, omniscient, renowned for his good deeds, pure, and ever responsive to devotion; meditating on his own essence.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	"Equal to Brahma, the Protector of his people, pleasing to look upon; supporting the universe; the destroyer of those who contravene the moral code; the inspirer of virtue; the giver of special grace to his devotees and to those who duly observe sacrificial rites and are charitable; conversant with the essence of the Vedic philosophy; an adept in the science of warfare; skilled in the scriptural law; of infallible memory; beloved of all; of courteous disposition; incapable of cowardice; acquainted with the laws of this world as also of the other worlds.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	"As the rivers hasten to the ocean, so do men of virtue ever approach him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	"Equal to Vishnu in valour; grateful to the sight as the full moon; when stirred to righteous anger, resembling allconsuming death; in patience like the earth, in generosity like Kuvera; in truthfulness the personification of virtue.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Such are his great qualities--Rama, the beloved heir of King Dasaratha, possessing every excellent attribute, benevolent to all, devoted to the welfare of every living being."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	His father, King Dasaratha, made preparations to install him as his regent, but the Queen Kaikeyi, claiming the boons formerly promised to her, demanded the exile of Rama and the enthronement of her own son Bharata.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The king held by his promise and by the ties of honour, sent his son Rama, whom he loved as his own life, into exile.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Obeying the command of his royal sire, and in order to gratify Kaikeyi, Shri Rama went to the forest.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The son of Queen Sumitra, Prince Lakshmana, inspired by affection and humility, followed his brother Rama into exile.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The daughter of King Janaka, an incarnation of Lakshmi, endowed with the highest feminine virtues, seeing Prince Lakshmana accompanying Rama, obedient to her lord, followed him as Venus follows the moon.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Accompanied for some leagues by King Dasaratha and his people, Rama dismissed the chariot on reaching the town of Shringavera on the banks of the Ganges, and commanded the minister Sumantra to return to the capital.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Here the prince met his beloved Guha, the chief of the Chandalas, accompanied by whom, with Lakshmana and Sita, he crossed the river Ganges and entered the forest, arriving at length at the Cittrakuta mountain described by the Sage Bharadvaja.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Rama, Lakshmana and Sita dwelt happily in the forest like devas or gandharvas.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Overwhelmed with grief at the separation from his sons and lamenting their absence, the king departed this life, while Rama was dwelling on the Cittrakuta mountain.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The holy sages offered the throne, left vacant on the death of King Dasaratha, to Prince Bharata, who declined it, not desiring the kingdom.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Setting forth to the forest where Shri Rama dwelt, in order to propitiate him, he approached that hero of truth with humility and directing his attention to the code of justice with which he was conversant, requested Rama to return and govern the kingdom.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The magnanimous, handsome and mighty Rama refused to accept the throne, preferring to carry out the command of his sire and, presenting Prince Bharata with his sandals as a symbol of authority, repeatedly exhorted him to return to the capital.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Shri Bharata, touching the feet of Rama in submission, departed and began to rule the dominion from the town of Nandigrama, while eagerly awaiting the return of his brother.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The sages and hermits, who dwelt in the forest, constantly harassed by asuras, approached Shri Ramacandra to ask for his protection--Shri Rama agreed to slay the evil asuras in order to preserve the Sages who had sought his help.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The holy men, whose appearance equalled the fire in lustre, heard of Shri Rama's resolve and were assured by him of his protection.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The female asura Shurpanakha, who could assume various forms at will, was overpowered and disfigured by Rama and Lakshmana.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	All the wicked rakshasas came led by Khara, Dushana and Trishira, to engage in combat with Shri Rama, and were slain by him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Shri Rama slew fourteen thousand rakshasas who dwelt in that forest.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Hearing of the slaughter of the rakshasas, King Ravana transported with rage, took with him Marica, a demon like himself.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Marica, knowing the superior strength of Rama, sought to dissuade Ravana from entering into combat with him, but Ravana who was marked down by destiny, disregarded the advice and went with Marica to Shri Rama's abode.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	There, Marica lured Shri Rama and Lakshmana away from the hermitage, and Ravana, having slain the vulture Jatayu, carried Sita away.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Learning from the dying Jatayu of the abduction of the daughter of the King of Mithila, Shri Rama was overwhelmed with grief and began to mourn.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Having performed the funeral rites of the vulture, while wandering in search of Sita, he encountered an asura named Kabandha whose form was menacing and terrible.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Shri Rama slew him and then performed the funeral rites whereupon his soul ascended to heaven.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	While passing to the celestial sphere, Kabandha spoke to Rama of Shabari, a female ascetic, and entreated him to visit her.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Shri Rama, the ever resplendent Destroyer of his foes, came to where Shabari dwelt and was duly worshipped by her.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	On the banks of the Lake Pampa, Shri Rama met the monkey Hanuman who presented Sugriva to him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The mighty Rama related the whole of his story to him as far as the abduction of Shri Sita.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Sugriva having listened to Shri Rama entered into the rite of friendship with him, witnessed by the fire.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	With full faith in Rama, Sugriva then recounted to him all the sufferings he had endured through his enmity with Bali and the great daring of the latter.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Then Shri Rama vowed to slay Bali, but Sugriva, uncertain of Rama's prowess and desiring to test him, showed him the bones of the body of Dundhubi, forming a heap as high as a mountain.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	With his foot, Rama kicked the heap to a distance of ten yojanas and, discharging an arrow, pierced seven palmyra trees, cleaving a mountain and with the shaft penetrating to the centre of the earth.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Having witnessed this exploit, Sugriva was satisfied, and thereafter trusted Rama implicitly.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	In his company he passed through deep valleys to the town of Kishkindhya; there, the yellow-eyed Sugriva roared like thunder.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	At this terrible sound, the powerful and valiant monkey chief, Bali, issued forth, disregarding the warning of his wife Tara, and engaged in combat with Sugriva.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	As desired by Sugriva, Shri Rama slew Bali with a single arrow; then he entrusted the government of Kishkindhya to Sugriva who now, as king of the monkey tribe, gathered his forces together and dispatched them to every quarter in search of Sita.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The vulture chief, the courageous Sampati, informed Hanuman where Sita was, whereupon the monkey leapt over the sea that lies between Bharatvarsh and Lanka, a distance of five hundred miles.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Entering the city of Lanka that was protected by Ravana, Hanuman beheld Sita, meditating on Rama in the ashoka garden.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	He there delivered Rama's ring to her and acquainted her with the welfare of her lord.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Having revived the courage of Sita, he shattered the gate of the garden and slew seven sons of the counsellors of Ravana, five great captains and levelled Akshyakumara, the son of Ravana, to the dust.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Then he suffered himself to be taken captive.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Knowing he could not be subdued by the weapon granted by Brahma to Ravana, yet acknowledging the power of its blessing, Hanuman allowed himself to be imprisoned, suffering many indignities.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Subsequently he burnt the whole of Lanka, only sparing the place where Sita dwelt.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Returning to deliver his welcome tidings, he respectfully circumambulated the mighty Rama and recounted in detail how he had found Sita.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Setting out in the company of Sugriva and others, Rama reached the sea.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	There he created a tempest by his shining arrows and the Lord of the waters, Sumudra, appeared before him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Under his direction, Nala threw a bridge over the sea.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Crossing the sea by means of this bridge, Shri Rama entered Lanka, slew Ravana in battle and recovered Sita, but she being the subject of slander, was addressed by him with harsh words in the midst of the assembly.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	After hearing the words of Rama with forbearance, Sita entered a great fire.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	On the testimony of the fire god, Sita was proved to be innocent and Rama, adored by all the gods, was content.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	The animate and inanimate beings of the three worlds, the gods and the sages, gave thanks that Ravana had been slain by Shri Rama.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Shri Rama enthroned Vibishana as the king of the asuras and, being wholly satisfied, revived all the monkeys and asuras who had fallen in battle.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	In the aerial chariot, Pushpaka, accompanied by Sugriva, Shri Rama, a devotee of truth, reached the hermitage of Bharadvaja.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	From there, he sent Hanuman to Prince Bharata, as his messenger and conversing with Sugriva again mounted the aerial chariot and arrived at Nandigrama.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Ever obedient to his father, Shri Rama then cut off his matted locks and with Sita occupied the throne of Ayodhya.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Seeing Shri Rama occupying the throne, the people were happy and satisfied, virtuous and free from sickness, sorrow, famine or danger.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	None witnessed the death of his son; no woman became a widow and all were devoted to their husbands; there was no danger from tempests; none perished by water; nor was there any cause of fear from fire; fever and plague were unknown; there was no want, and no danger from thieves.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Cities and villages were rich and prosperous; all lived happily as in the Satya Yuga.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Shri Rama and Sita observed countless Vedic sacrifices and gave much gold, and hundreds of thousands of cows in charity, thus preparing for themselves a place in the divine regions.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	Shri Rama added incalculably to the prosperity of the dynasty, and bestowed immense wealth on the brahmins.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	He employed his subjects in the duties of their respectives castes and ruled for eleven thousand years, after which he returned to his celestial abode, Vaikuntha.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	He who reads the story of Rama, which imparts merit and purity, is freed from all sin.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	He who reads it with faith and devotion is ultimately worshipped together with his sons, grandsons and servants at his death.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	01_Shri Narada relates to Valmiki the story of Rama	A brahmin reading this becomes proficient in the Vedas, and philosophy; a kshatriya becomes a king; a vaishya grows prosperous in trade; a shudra, on reading this will become great in his caste.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The wise and eloquent Valmiki with his disciple, Bharadvaja, having listened to the words of Narada, was filled with wonder and worshipped Rama in his heart.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	He offered obeisance to Shri Narada, who craved permission to depart and on his request being granted he ascended through space to the heavens.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Narada, having departed, the great Muni Valmiki proceeded to the banks of the river Tamasa, which was close to the Ganges.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Reaching that place and seeing the pure and limpid waters, Valmiki said to his disciple: "O Bharadvaja, behold how pure is the water of the holy river, verily it is clear and pleasant like the mind of a good man.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	O Child, set down the waterpot and fetch me my bark robe from the hermitage.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	I wish to bathe in the sacred stream, delay not."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Obedient to the command of his Guru, the disciple brought the raiment from the Sage's hermitage and returning speedily, offered it to him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Receiving the robe of bark from the hands of his disciple, the sage, with his senses fully controlled, girded it about him and while bathing repeated the traditional prayers, offering libations of water to his ancestors and the gods.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Then he wandered about in the forest enjoying the beauties of nature.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Now the august sage, Shri Valmiki, beheld a pair of Krauncha birds fearlessly disporting themselves in love.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Soon after, a fowler stealing up unobserved, slew the male bird in the presence of the sage.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The female bird, deprived of her yellow crested companion, who but now had been spreading his wings in the act of love to please her, perceiving him bleeding and crying out in distress, began to mourn.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The heart of the sage was filled with pity on seeing the bird struck down by the fowler.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Touched by the lament of the female krauncha and incensed by the cruel act of the fowler, the sage said: "O Fowler, having killed the bird in the midst of the enjoyment of love with its mate, you shall never attain prosperity.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Do not visit the forest for many years lest evil overtake you."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Reflecting on the words he had addressed to the fowler and realising their implication, the sage said to himself: "What words are these that I have uttered, inspired by my compassion for the dying bird?"
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The wise and learned sage reflected a moment, and then said to his disciple: "Grieving for the dying bird, I have recited this verse of four feet, each of equal syllables, which can be sung to the vina.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	May it bring me renown and may no ill be spoken of me on account of this."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	With great delight the disciple committed to memory the verse composed by his spiritual preceptor, who expressed his satisfaction at the skill of his pupil Bharadvaja.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Bathing in the sacred river, according to the prescribed ritual, the sage returned to his hermitage, pondering over the matter.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The humble and learned disciple Bharadvaja followed the great Sage, carrying his loshta filled with water.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	On entering the hermitage, the sage worshipped the Lord and performed other rituals and having instructed his disciple in the tradition and the sacred history, passed into deep meditation.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The Creator of the world, the Self-born, the fourfaced and glorious Brahma at length appeared before the holy sage.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Valmiki rose hastily, filled with astonishment, and welcoming the Deity in great humility, offered obeisance to Him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Leading Him to a seat, in profound reverence he poured forth libations of water as enjoined in the tradition, making enquiries as to His welfare.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The Blessed Lord accepted the homage offered to Him and commanded the sage to be seated.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Shri Valmiki occupied the place designated by Brahma and once more recollected his grief over the incident of the wicked fowler, who ruthlessly slew the bird that was so happy and cooing with delight.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	He recalled the grief of the female bird and read and re-read the lines:--
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	"By the ignorant and wicked fowler, grief is born
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	For he has wantonly slain the melodious krauncha."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Shri Brahma, seeing the sage afflicted and sorrowful, said to him: "O Great Sage, let these words spontaneously uttered by you, inspired by the death of the krauncha, be poetry.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Do you describe the whole story of Rama, who is the essence of virtue and full of the highest attributes, in accordance with what you have heard from Shri Narada.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Do you narrate all the known and hitherto unknown deeds of Shri Rama, Sita and Lakshmana and the asuras.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Whatever relates to King Dasaratha, his wives, city, palace, sayings, conduct and what he accomplished, will be revealed to you by my favour.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	None of your words will prove false.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Do you render into verse the sacred and delightful deeds of Rama.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	O Sage, as long as the mountains and rivers remain on the earth, so long will the story of Shri Rama endure.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	So long as the story of Rama endures, so long shalt you abide in the higher regions."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Having uttered these words, Shri Brahma pondered awhile within Himself and then vanished from sight.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	The great sage and his disciple were filled with amazement at this event, and reading the stanza again and again, their delight grew.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Repeatedly reciting the couplet, composed by Valmiki, they realised that the holy sage had expressed lbs sorrow in poetic form.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Then Shri Valmiki meditated on the Lord within his soul and it occurred to him to relate the story of Rama in similar verse.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	For the good of the world, the illustrious and holy sage, therefore, began composing the life of Shri Rama in verse; that Rama, worthy of world-wide renown, who is both generous and charming.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	02_Sage Valmiki creates the metrical form for the story	Shri Valmiki composed the story of the life of Rama and of the slaying of Ravana in beautiful and measured stanzas, a work of infinite merit.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	03_The deeds of Rama that will be described in the sacred poem	Having heard the story of the life of the sagacious Rama from the lips of Shri Narada which, when recounted, confers perfect righteousness on the hearer, the holy sage wished to know more concerning the sacred theme.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	03_The deeds of Rama that will be described in the sacred poem	Washing his hands and feet and drinking a little pure water, placing himself facing the east on a seat of kusha grass, with joined palms, he passed into profound meditation and in a vision beheld the history of Rama.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	03_The deeds of Rama that will be described in the sacred poem	Through the grace of Shri Brahma, the holy sage saw all that Rama, Sita and Lakshmana had experienced, observed and done.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	03_The deeds of Rama that will be described in the sacred poem	He witnessed in detail the life of Rama, who was truth incarnate and all that he had accomplished in the forest and other places.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	03_The deeds of Rama that will be described in the sacred poem	By the power of spiritual meditation and yoga, the Sage Valmiki saw the whole past as clearly as if it were a fruit placed on the palm of his hand.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	03_The deeds of Rama that will be described in the sacred poem	Thus, having witnessed all, the most enlightened sage began to describe the life of Shri Rama in verse.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	03_The deeds of Rama that will be described in the sacred poem	The history of Shri Rama, which confers righteousness, worldly prosperity and delight on the reader, which does not degrade the mind and grants release from sorrow, that story which charms the heart and is as full of lovely gems as is the sea, was rendered by Shri Valmiki, in the form in which Shri Narada had related it to him.

RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	While Shri Rama was still King of Ayodhya, the great Sage Valmiki composed this beautiful classic.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The holy rishi composed twenty-four thousand verses and divided them into five hundred chapters and six books.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	In addition, he composed the epilogue.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The work being completed, he reflected thus: "To whom shall I teach this classic?"
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	While the sage was reflecting on the matter, the two princes, Kusha and Lava, the offspring of Rama and Sita approached him and touched his feet in reverence.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The great sage studied these two virtuous princes of mellifluous speech, who dwelt with him in his hermitage at that time.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Knowing them to be wise and full of faith in the teachings of the Vedas, the great sage, who had expounded the meaning of the scriptures in his verses, taught the classic to them.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The great Valmiki taught them the classic describing the deeds of Rama and Sita and all that relates to the incidents leading to the slaying of Ravana named "The Slaying of the Grandson of Paulastya".
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	This historical classic is pleasant to sing and adapted to the three measures of time, it is contained within the seven notes and can be sung to the vina.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	It expresses the various moods of love, courage, disgust, anger, terror, compassion, wonder, laughter and serenity.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The two princes were skilled musicians, proficient in rhythm and melody and had sweet voices; they were as comely to look at as Gandharvas.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Endowed with god-like beauty, the two sweet singers, the reflected images of Shri Rama himself, constantly repeated the holy classic and committed it to memory.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The two adorable and charming princes skilfully recited the holy classic, the Ramayana, which extols virtue, before the sages, the learned brahmins and the ascetics, as they had been instructed to do.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	On a particular occasion, the two princes, great-souled, fortunate, and equipped with all good qualities, chanted the great epic in Shri Rama's assembly.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The listening sages were visibly moved and shed tears of delight.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Being overcome with wonder, they cried "Excellent!
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Excellent", and praising the two singers, the virtue-loving sages experienced great joy.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Showering praises on the brothers, they cried, "How melodiously you sing!
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	How exquisite is the divine poem, the story of Rama!"
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Being pleased with the sweet singers, one sage presented them with loshtas, another with delicious fruits, a third with robes of bark and another with antelope skins; some gave sacrificial thread, some vessels for collecting alms, others gave loin cloths, kusha grass, garments of yellow cloth, scarves and thread for binding the hair, sacrificial vessels, rosaries and axes.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Others bestowed their blessings upon them, saying "May you live long" and all acclaimed the author of the marvellous poem.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	They said: "This metre will be the foundation of the verse of future poets; it is composed according to specific rules; the two princes have sung this wonderful poem with great art; it will promote wisdom in those who listen to it and grant them longevity and health; it is truly able to charm the heart."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	While the sages were thus praising the two princes, Shri Ramacandra, passing that way, took them to his royal palace.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Occupying his golden throne, Shri Rama, the destroyer of his foes, offered hospitality and reverence to the two worthy princes.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	In the assembly, surrounded by his ministers and brothers, Shri Rama looked approvingly on those handsome and learned youths, and addressed the Princes Lakshmana, Shatrughna and Bharata saying: "Hear the historical poem, which these two celestial and brilliant minstrels sing, this poem which portrays incidents of wonderful meaning."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Then Shri Rama commanded the two musicians to sing and the princes tuned their vinas and chanted the poem they had learned, sweetly and clearly.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	The whole assembly listened to the music which was wholly gratifying to the mind and heart.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Shri Rama said: "I admire the music and the verse sung by these two minstrels who appear to be endowed with royal attributes."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	In this way, praised and encouraged by Shri Ramacandra, the two brothers demonstrating their skill in music, sang on.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	04_Shri Rama's sons chant the poem	Listening to them in the royal assembly, Shri Ramacandra was charmed.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	The earth consisting of seven islands has been under one ruler since the time of those kings descended from Manu, who were ever victorious.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	Among those mighty monarchs was Sagara followed by his sixty thousand sons who hollowed out the ocean.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	This classic Ramayana contains the history of the House of Sagara, founded by Ikshvaku.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	This Rama-Katha will be recited from beginning to end--let all listen to it with faith.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	On the banks of the river Sarayu, there was a great and prosperous country named Koshala, inhabited by contented people.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	In it was the city of Ayodhya, famous in the three worlds, founded by the renowned Manu, a lord among men.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	The city's thoroughfares extended for sixty miles; its beauty was enhanced by streets admirably planned, the principal highways being sprinkled with water and strewn with flowers.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	King Dasaratha protected the city as Maghavan protects Amaravati.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	He dwelt there in splendour, as Indra in heaven.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	The city had beautiful and massive gates and charming markets; its fortifications were planned by skilful engineers and artificers.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	There were bards, ballad singers and public musicians in the city; the inhabitants were wealthy and had spacious houses with high arched porticos, decorated with flags and banners.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	It was filled with extensive buildings and beautiful gardens, and surrounded by mango groves, tall trees enhancing the outskirts of the city, giving it the appearance of a beautiful girl wearing a girdle of greenery.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	The city was enclosed by strong fortifications and a deep moat which no enemy, by any expedient whatsoever, could penetrate.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	Countless elephants, horses, cattle, camels and mules were to be seen in the city.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	Innumerable ambassadors and merchants dwelt there and people from many lands traded peacefully within its walls.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	Ayodhya, like Indra's Amaravati, was resplendent with gilded palaces, the walls of which were set with precious stones, the domes resembling mountain peaks.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	Gem-encrusted, sky-kissing buildings could be seen throughout the royal capital.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	Dwelling houses, tall and fair, stood in well-placed sites and resounded with delightful music.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	There were lovely dwellings occupied by men of noble birth, resembling the aerial chariots that carry those of pure fife and spiritual perfection to heaven.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	The warriors living in that city were of those who do not slay a fleeing foe, they were skilled archers, able to pierce a target by sound alone.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	Many had slain tigers, lions and wolves wandering near their homes, either in single combat or with different kinds of weapons.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	This great city which harboured thousands of chieftains was built by King Dasaratha.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	05_King Dasaratha's kingdom and capital	In Ayodhya lived countless learned men engaged in the observance of rituals, there were also artists and craftsmen, men deeply read in the Veda and those endowed with every virtue, full of truth and wisdom, as well as thousands of seers and sages versed in the mystical science of Yoga.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	There dwelt in that city, King Dasaratha, a follower of the tradition of the illustrious Emperor Manu.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	The king was learned in the interpretation of the Vedas, his chief wealth was pre-eminence in truth and virtue; he was one who never broke his word, who was ever prudent, majestic and beloved of his subjects, a great charioteer, a worthy descendant of the dynasty of Ikshvaku, an observer of many sacrifices, one who ever delighted in the practice of righteousness; in full authority over his people, equal to a great sage; a royal seer, renowned in the three worlds, triumphing over his enemies, a friend to all; having perfect control of his senses and appetites; in prosperity equal to Indra; in wealth equal to Kuvera.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	That truth-loving monarch, striving to acquire perfection in virtue, worldly prosperity and happiness, ruled the city as the celestial monarch Indra rules Amaravati.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	The people in that city were happy, virtuous, learned, experienced, each satisfied with his state, practising his own calling, without avarice and of truthful speech.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	None was indigent or dwelt in a mean habitation; all lived happily with their families, possessing wealth, grain, cattle and horses.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	In that city of Ayodhya, none was a miser or a swindler, none was mean-spirited, proud, rash, worthless or an atheist.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	Men and women were of righteous conduct, fully self-controlled, and in their pure and chaste behaviour they equalled the great sages.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	None lacked earrings, coronets and necklaces.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	They bathed daily and rubbed their bodies with oil, using attar of roses and sandal paste.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	None ate impure food, none allowed his neighbour to suffer hunger.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	All possessed ornaments and gold, and there was none who had not learnt to subdue his mind.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	No one in the city neglected to offer butter and fragrant objects in the sacrificial fire.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	No one was mean, impious or failed to discharge his duties; there were no thieves and none were born of mixed castes.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	The brahmins were devoted to their respective duties, firm in self-control and authorized to accept gifts.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	None denied the existence of God, none uttered falsehood or were enamoured of worldly pleasure and none was guilty of slander.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	No brahmin was unversed in the six systems of philosophy nor did any neglect to fast at the full moon, or on other appointed days; there were none who suffered from mental or physical infirmities and none were unhappy in that city.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	Among the inhabitants, there were no revolutionaries and none who were not loyal to king and state.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	Those who dwelt there, worshipped the gods and the uninvited guest; they were both magnanimous and charitable.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	All attained a ripe age as virtuous and truth-loving people; their homes were filled with children, grandchildren and virtuous women.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	The warriors were subject to the learned brahmins and the merchants to the warrior caste; in accordance with their caste the people served the brahmins, the warriors and the merchants.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	In the administration of the empire, the Emperor Dasaratha followed the example of the first ruler Manu who was supreme in wisdom and a god among men.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	Ayodhya abounded in warriors, undefeated in battle, fearless and skilful in the use of arms, resembling lions guarding their mountain caves.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	There were horses in the city from Kamroja, Vanaya, Nudi and Vahli, and elephants from the regions of Vindhu and Himavat.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	The city of Ayodhya was full of courageous and noble men belonging to the races of Bhadra, Mulla and Mriga, inhabitants of the regions of Bincyachala and the Himalayan ranges.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	The city possessed mighty elephants like great hills.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	That capital was truly worthy of the name 'Ayodhya,' which means "The city none can challenge in warfare".
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	Dwelling there, the Emperor Dasaratha, ruling the kingdom, resembled the moon in the midst of countless stars.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	06_The city of Ayodhya	That great king, equal to Indra himself, reigned over the city, guarded by fortifications and ramparts, a city which contained innumerable dwellings of many kinds and thousands of prosperous inhabitants.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Ever devoted to the welfare of King Dasaratha, the ministers of the House of Ikshvaku were possessed of all the virtues; their counsels were based on truth and they understood the import of the royal commands immediately.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Eight of the king's counsellors were famed; untiringly employed in the affairs of state, they were honest and devoted to the cultivation of virtue.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Their names were Dhristi [Dhrishti], Jayanta, Vijaja [Vijaya], Siddhartha, Atyartha-Sadaka [Arthasadhaka], Ashoka, Mantra-pala and Sumantra.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	The great and holy sages, Vasishtha and Vamadeva assisted the king in his observance of spiritual duties and also acted as his advisers.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	All the ministers were virtuous, scorning to do wrong, benevolent, versed in the moral law, of wide experience, disinterested, magnanimous, acquainted with the spirit of the scriptures, forbearing, patient, obedient to the king, true to their word, cheerful, free from avarice and well acquainted with the affairs of their fellow subjects and with those of the subjects of other monarchs.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	They were efficient, firm in friendship, and even passed judgment on their own sons if they broke the law.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	These counsellors were expert in the science of economics and warfare, and never inflicted unmerited punishment on an enemy.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	They were brave and unambitious.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Conversant with every branch of political life, they protected all those who lived in the state.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Adding to the royal treasury without burdening the learned and the warriors, they inflicted penalties on wrongdoers with due regard to their capacity for bearing it.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	These ministers were pure of heart and of chaste conduct.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	None consorted with his neighbour's wife, none were wicked and all lived together peaceably.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Cultivating every good quality and practising the various arts, they were renowned for their courage, their fair name was published abroad and their lives were guided by reason.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Skilled in the laws of the country and blessed with wealth, they issued wise edicts and exercised their minds in philosophical debate.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Acquainted with the moral code, they conversed affectionately with each other; such were King Dasaratha's ministers who, informed by their agents of the needs of the people, satisfied them and governed with prudence.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	In the administration of his kingdom, the king never permitted unrighteousness to cause dissension, and became known throughout the world as an ocean of truth.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	That lion among men King Dasaratha, reigning over the earth, had none superior or equal to himself.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Honoured by his feudal lords, surrounded by friends, King Dasaratha, like Indra, reigned in majesty.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	07_The administration of the kingdom (Ayodhya)	Benevolent, powerful, accomplished and gracious, King Dasaratha protected Ayodhya and shone in splendour like the sun illumining the world.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	King Dasaratha, that glorious and righteous king, though performing great austerities, was without an heir to the throne.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Then the wise and great-souled monarch said to himself: "I will perform the horse-sacrifice (Asva-medha) in order to have a son."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Having thus decided, the supremely sagacious sovereign convened a meeting of his counsellors and addressing his chief minister, Sumantra, commanded him as follows: "Send speedily for the spiritual preceptors and priests."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Quick to act, Sumantra at once summoned those highly learned preceptors and brought thither Suyagna, Vamadeva, Javali, Kasyapa and Vasishtha together with other eminent priests and brahmins.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Having offered salutations to these holy men, King Dasaratha, speaking in gracious accents, uttered words full of truth and purpose: He said, "O Sages, I have practised virtue and yet I have not had the good fortune to be blessed with a son; it is therefore my intention to perform the horse-sacrifice.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	I wish to act according to the injunction of the scriptures; you, O Holy Men, advise me after due deliberation as to how I can be successful in the proposed undertaking".
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	The learned brahmins, led by Shri Vasishtha, praised the king's intention and said: "You have decided on the proper course, O King."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Highly pleased, they commanded those things requisite for the sacrifice to be assembled and the horse loosed.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	They said, "O King, let a place of sacrifice be chosen on the north bank of the river Sarayu.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	O King, this holy resolve formed by you, for the sake of an heir, will assuredly bring the fulfilment of your desire".
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Hearing the words of the brahmins, the monarch rejoiced and commanded his ministers to bring the sacrificial appointments and release the horse under the protection of the warriors; they were also directed to erect a sacrificial pavilion on the bank of the river Sarayu.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	He further decreed the adoption of those measures which would diminish the possibility of hindrance to the sacrifice, for even for kings, the horse-sacrifice was not easily performed.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	The king said: "Let it be remembered that during the observance of the sacrifice, no suffering must be inflicted on any, lest some perverse and crafty brahmin should cause obstruction in the proceedings.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	By carrying through the ritual without regard for scriptural injunctions, it comes to nought; therefore, bring the sacrifice to a successful conclusion.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	I depend on you, and expect you to carry the sacrifice through to a successful issue."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	The counsellors replied, saying, "O King, be it so".
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Blessing the monarch, the learned brahmins retired, and the king addressed his ministers saying: "Prepare the sacrifice as the officiating priests have instructed you and accept responsibility for its final success."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	Then the illustrious sovereign left the court and entered his private apartments where the queens dwelt, who loved the king from the depths of their hearts.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	King Dasaratha addressed them, saying: "I intend to observe a sacrifice for the sake of obtaining a son, do you all follow the prescribed discipline."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	08_King Dasaratha desires to perform a sacrifice for the birth of a son	The queens rejoiced to hear these words from the lips of the king and their lotus-like faces brightened like flowers on the departure of the cold season.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	Sumantra, having heard of the preparations for the sacrifice, obtained a private audience with his sovereign and said: "I have heard of a tradition, formerly related to me by the august brahmins.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	O King, in ancient days, the blessed Sanatkumara predicted to the holy sages around him that a son would be born to you.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	It was prophesied that a son of Kasyapa, named Vibhandaka would have a son called Rishyasringa and that he should dwell in the forest alone with his saintly father, unknown to any other man or woman.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	This sage would keep the twofold vow of brahmacarya enjoined by the sages.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	In this way he would pass a long time worshipping God through the fire-sacrifice and the service of his sire.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	In the country named Anga, a famous king named Lomapada, would oppress the people by his evil way of life and thus cause a drought.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	On account of this, the king would suffer great affliction and summoning the brahmins would say to them: "O Wise Men, acquainted as you are with the customs of the world and also the divine laws, tell me what ritual of purification and repentance I can adopt to expiate my evil deeds, which have brought about this drought."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	Then the brahmins, learned in the Veda, would answer the king thus: "O King, exert thyself by every means to bring the son of the Sage Vibhandaka hither.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	Having with due reverence conveyed him hither, do you confer your daughter Shanta on him in marriage."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	The king having listened to their words and reflected on how he should bring that excellent sage to the court, would then request his ministers and priests to approach the sage, but they would declare their unwillingness to undertake the mission, being afraid of the rishi's power.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	In order to avoid the monarch's displeasure, however, after deliberating on the method by which the sage could be brought to the court, they would make the following proposal: "By the courtesans can the sage be persuaded to come to the king's court, the rains will then follow and the drought will be at an end.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	Then will the king join his daughter in marriage to the sage.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	By pouring oblations into the sacrificial fire the illustrious sage, Rishyasringa, will, by his grace, obtain the desired son for King Dasaratha."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	"Thus spoke the illustrious Sanatkumara, in the midst of the sages, and I have now recounted it to you."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	09_Sumantra relates a tradition that a son will be born through the help of the Sage Rishyasringa	King Dasaratha was delighted to hear these words, and requested the minister to describe further how King Lomapada brought the sage to his court.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Thus requested, Sumantra began to narrate the story in detail and said: "O Great King, hear how the ministers brought the Sage Rishyasringa to the court.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	"The ministers addressed King Lomapada saying:
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	'We have a plan whereby the young sage may be conveyed hither successfully.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	He resides in the forest, devoted to holy study, spiritual practices and asceticism, and is wholly unacquainted with the pursuit of pleasure.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	"'By the means of those things gratifying to the senses, we shall most certainly be able to bring the sage to the court.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Let beautifully-attired and lovely courtesans go there and by their acts, charm and bring him hither'."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The king approved the plan and commanded his ministers to carry it out.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The courtesans then entered the forest and took up their abode near the hermitage, seeking a meeting with the young sage.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Protected by his father, the youthful ascetic seldom passed the boundaries of the hermitage, nor had he seen any man or woman beyond its precincts.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	One day, impelled by destiny, the youth went forth from the hermitage and beheld the graceful and beautiful women, attired in many-coloured robes of exquisite design, singing sweetly.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	They approached the son of Rishi Vibhandaka and addressed him, saying: "Who art you?
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Whose son art you?
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	What is your name?
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Why dost you dwell in the dark forest?"
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Never having beheld women of beauty and charm before, Rishyasringa was captivated and answered them, saying: "My father is the great Sage Vibhandaka of the family of Kasyapa and I am his son, my name is Rishyasringa.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	O Beautiful Beings of charming mien, my hermitage is near at hand, please come thither and allow me to offer you hospitality there."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The courtesans accepted the invitation and accompanied the sage who received them in the traditional manner, placing before them water to wash their feet and delicious roots and fruits.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Fearing the father's return and anxious to depart with all haste, the courtesans plied the young sage with tasty confections which they had brought with them, saying: "Be pleased to accept these dainties which we have brought for you to enjoy on this occasion."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	They then caressed the youth, feeding him with sweets and other delicacies.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The resplendent sage partook of the offerings, thinking them to be fruits, never having tasted any other food.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The courtesans, fearing the father's return, pretended to be fasting and left the hermitage.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	At their departure, the youthful sage felt dejected and restless.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The following day, the courtesans, charmingly attired, again went to the hermitage and smiled on perceiving the young sage appear so disconsolate.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	They then approached him and said: "O Handsome Youth, to-day please grace our hermitage with your presence.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	O Auspicious One, we can entertain you better there than here."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The young sage agreed to accompany them and went with them to their abode.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	As the sage entered the city, Indra showered rain on the domain of King Lomapada and the people rejoiced.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	When the rain began to fall, King Lomapada, realising that the holy sage had entered the city, went out to meet him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Offering him humble and loving salutations, he presented him with the traditional gifts (arghya) of water and food, and entreated him to grant the boon that his father Vibhandaka should not visit his displeasure on him.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	The king then took the youth to the inner apartments and united him in marriage to his daughter Shanta.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	10_Sumantra He describes how Rishyasringa was brought to King Lomapada's court	Deeply revered by the king, Rishyasringa lived happily in the capital with his bride, the Princess Shanta.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Sumantra said: "O Great King, hearken further to the words of the great Sage Sanatkumara:--
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	"'In the House of Ikshvaku, there will be a highly righteous and truth-loving king named Dasaratha who will form an alliance with King Lomapada of Anga.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	"'King Dasaratha will approach his friend Lomapada and beg the assistance of Rishyasringa, the husband of the Princess Shanta, in the performance of the sacrifice he desires to observe, that he may be blessed with a son.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	After mature consideration, King Lomapada will permit Shanta's lord, Rishyasringa to accompany King Dasaratha.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Highly gratified, King Dasaratha will return to his capital with Rishyasringa and will ask the sage to officiate at the sacrifice he is about to perform in order to obtain sons and also a future abode in the celestial regions.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	"'As a result of the sacrifice, King Dasaratha will have four sons, each of limitless valour.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	These sons will be renowned throughout the world and will increase the glory of their dynasty.'
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	"This story was narrated by the Sage Sanatkumara in the first quarter of Satya-Yuga.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	O Great King!
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	You should approach Rishyasringa with a worthy chariot and retinue, and bring him with ceremony to your capital."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Having heard the good counsel of his minister Sumantra, the King commanded him to inform his Guru Vasishtha of this matter, and the holy Vasishtha acquiesced in the plan.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Then the king, with firm resolve, attended by his queens, counsellors and priests, prepared to set forth for the city where Rishyasringa dwelt.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Passing through various forests and traversing many rivers, the king arrived at Lomapada's capital.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	There he beheld the resplendent sage, in lustre like a glowing fire, seated near King Lomapada.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Inspired by friendship, the great monarch Lomapada offered respectful salutations to King Dasaratha and informed Rishyasringa of his alliance with this king, whereupon the sage expressed his approval in words of praise.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Having enjoyed the hospitality of King Lomapada for seven days, King Dasaratha addressed him thus: "O King, I desire to enter upon an important undertaking, be gracious enough to allow your daughter Shanta and her lord to return to my capital to assist me."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Hearing these words, King Lomapada replied: "Be it so," and turning to the sage said: "Be pleased to go with your wife to the capital of King Dasaratha."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	The youthful sage assented to the command of King Lomapada, and he, in company with his spouse, departed with King Dasaratha.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Having taken leave of his friend, King Dasaratha despatched speedy messengers to go before him to instruct his ministers to prepare for their arrival.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	The people of Ayodhya carried out all as they had been commanded and overjoyed at the monarch's return, fulfilled the instructions of his messengers.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	The citizens were delighted to behold the young sage entering the city and being honoured by the king, as Indra in heaven pays tribute to Kasyapa.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Having introduced the sage and his consort to the inner apartments, the king offered him the traditional welcome as enjoined in the scriptures.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	The royal ladies also welcomed the wide-eyed Shanta with her lord to the private apartments, and expressed their pleasure and delight.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	11_King Dasaratha goes to King Lomapada, by whose permission Rishyasringa comes to Ayodhya	Honoured and worshipped by the queens, no less than by King Dasaratha himself, the Princess Shanta and her husband, the sage, dwelt in the palace as Brihaspati resides in the city of Mahendra.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	Time passed and the spring came again while the holy sage was at the court of King Dasaratha.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	On a propitious day, the king decided to enter upon the sacrifice.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	He approached Rishyasringa and, bowing low, offered salutations to him, inviting that god-like sage to assist in the sacrifice he was observing, to preserve the dynasty.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	The sage agreed and requested the king to provide the necessary material for the sacrifice and to let loose the horse.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	The sovereign commanded his minister Sumantra to summon with all speed the priests acquainted with the philosophy of the Veda, and sent invitations to the sages Vamadeva, Javali, Kasyapa, the high priest Vasishtha and other exalted and learned brahmins.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	Sumantra, setting out in haste, approached the sages courteously and brought them to the king.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	The virtuous monarch, after paying respectful homage to them, addressed them humbly, speaking words full of candour and integrity.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	He said: "O Sages, despite my ardent desire to have an heir, I am without one.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	I have, therefore, decided to perform the horse sacrifice to that end.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	I desire the sacrifice to be observed according to the scriptural laws and through the grace of the Sage Rishyasringa, I hope to attain my purpose."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	The sages advised the king to gather together the sacrificial articles and to release the horse.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	They said: "Righteous is your desire to be blessed with a son; O King, you shalt surely obtain four illustrious sons of limitless valour."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	The brahmins' words convinced the king that heirs would be granted to him and he communicated his satisfaction to his ministers.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	He said: "O Counsellors, bring together four high priests and set the horse at liberty under the protection of four hundred warriors.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	Let a sacrificial pavilion be set up on the bank of the river Sarayu, and let appropriate protective rites be observed lest obstructions arise."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	The king then ordained that during the period of sacrifice neither priests nor other persons should be subject to any suffering whatsoever.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	He said: "In such rites, others have been impeded by sub-human beings, which has resulted in the annulment of the sacrifice.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	You should, therefore, employ every means to bring the sacrifice to a successful conclusion."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	Hearing the words of the king, the ministers--highly gratified--began to act according to his instructions.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	Then the brahmins assured the king that the sacrifice would be accomplished without hindrance and offering him obeisance, returned to their homes.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	12_Rishyasringa agrees to assist in the sacrifice	The brahmins having departed, the king bade farewell to his ministers and entered his private apartments.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	The following year, spring having returned once more, the king, desiring to complete the sacrifice for the sake of an heir, paid homage to Shri Vasishtha, offering him humble salutations according to the prescribed ordinance, and addressed that great brahmin with submission, saying:--
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	"O Great Sage, be pleased to complete the holy ceremony according to the sacred tradition.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Let it be so undertaken that no interference may take place.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	You are compassionate and your heart is inclined towards me.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	You are also my Guru, the burden of the sacrifice must be borne by you."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	The most excellent sage replied, "Be it so.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	I will do as you desirest."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Hereafter, Shri Vasishtha summoned those brahmins,.able to perform the holy rituals and also artificers, architects, writers, actors and dancers.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Addressing the learned priests, he said: "At the king's command, inaugurate the great sacrifice.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Cause bricks in thousands to be brought hither with all speed and erect many kinds of dwellings, well arranged, furnished with food and every comfort to accommodate royal and other guests.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Prepare hundreds of beautiful houses on suitable sites, together with provisions and all things needed by brahmins; erect also large buildings for the people of other lands, and store food and articles of comfort where it is best to do so.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Fine and well-equipped houses should be built for villagers.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Ensure that hospitality in the form of food and refreshment be given with courtesy and kindness.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Those attending the sacrifice should be entertained with respect and consideration, being received in a becoming manner, according to their caste.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Let no affront be offered to any through greed, anger or lust.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Let craftsmen and servants be suitably regarded, so that their hearts be set on their task and let no one act disruptively.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Treat all in a spirit of goodwill and courtesy, so that the work may be successfully accomplished."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	The people listened to the holy sage and answered, "We will act according to your instructions, O Sage, nothing shall be omitted."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Shri Vasishtha then summoned the chief minister Sumantra and said: "Send out invitations to the sacrifice to all the righteous kings of the earth and also the brahmins, kshatriyas, vaishyas and shudras of every country, but go first to the great Sovereign of Mithila, the heroic Janaka, eminent in truth, the greatest of warriors and a knower of the Veda, since he is an ancient ally of King Dasaratha.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Thereafter, bring the evertruthful King of Kashi, of exemplary conduct, equal to a god; and then the aged and virtuous King of Kaikeya, our sovereign's father-in-law, and invite his son also.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Call the fortunate King Lomapada of Anga, the intimate friend of the King, and bring hither, with respect, Koshala, the King of Magadha.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	"Thereafter, send messengers to the kings of the eastern countries of Sindhu, Souriva, and Sourashtra, and the monarchs of the south, with other great kings of the earth; let them come with their brothers, relations, retainers and servants."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Having heard the words of Shri Vasishtha, Sumantra carried out the instructions given by him, dispatching invitations by special messengers to the monarchs of many lands, himself going forth to escort some of the great kings.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Sumantra having departed, all the workers employed in the sacrifice informed the holy sage of their progress, and he advised them further saying: "Let nothing be presented to any without due respect, even in jest; gifts given with contempt lead to the destruction of the giver."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	A few days later, the kings from afar arrived at the sacrificial pavilion bearing gifts of gems.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Then Shri Vasishtha, being pleased, said: "O King, at your command, all the kings have come and been received by me with due hospitality.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	The preparations for the sacrifice are now completed, be pleased to enter the sacrificial pavilion and inspect the articles needed for the ceremony.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	See how well your servants have furnished everything requisite and have gratified your every wish."
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	On the recommendation of the Sage Vasishtha and Rishyasringa, King Dasaratha went to the sacrificial ground at an auspicious time, when a propitious star was in the ascendant.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	Then the learned brahmins and Shri Vasishtha elected Rishyasringa as chief priest.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	13_The Sacrifice is commenced	The sacrifice began in accordance with the ancient ordinance and the king, with his queens, engaged in the preliminary initiations.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	14_The Ceremonies are performed with the appropriate rites	Having ranged far and wide during a year, the horse returned and on the bank of the river Sarayu the sacrifice of King Dasaratha continued.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	14_The Ceremonies are performed with the appropriate rites	The chief priests, under Rishyasringa, assisted the king in the observance of the rituals.
RAMA	01_Bala-kanda	14_The Ceremonies are performed with the appropriate rites	Brahmins learned in the ancient science, also officiated and assisted the king according to the instructions laid down in the Kalpa Sutra.
